________________________________________________________________________

To upgrade automatically, use MandrakeUpdate.

If you want to upgrade manually, download the updated package from one
of our FTP server mirrors and upgrade with "rpm -Fvh *.rpm".

You can download the updates directly from one of the mirror sites
listed at:

  http://www.linux-mandrake.com/en/ftp.php3.

Updated packages are available in the "updates/[ver]/RPMS/" directory.
For example, if you are looking for an updated RPM package for
Linux-Mandrake 7.2, look for it in "updates/7.2/RPMS/".  Updated source
RPMs are available as well, but you generally do not need to download
them.

Please be aware that sometimes it takes the mirrors a few hours to
update.

You can view other security advisories for Linux-Mandrake at:

  http://www.linux-mandrake.com/en/security/

If you want to report vulnerabilities, please contact

  security@linux-mandrake.com
________________________________________________________________________

Linux-Mandrake has two security-related mailing list services that
anyone can subscribe to:

security-announce@linux-mandrake.com

  Linux-Mandrake's security announcements mailing list.  Only
  announcements are sent to this list and it is read-only.

security-discuss@linux-mandrake.com

  Linux-Mandrake's security discussion mailing list.  This list is open
  to anyone to discuss Linux-Mandrake security specifically and Linux
  security in general.

To subscribe to either list, send a message to
  sympa@linux-mandrake.com
with "subscribe [listname]" in the body of the message.

To remove yourself from either list, send a message to
  sympa@linux-mandrake.com
with "unsubscribe [listname]" in the body of the message.

To get more information on either list, send a message to
  sympa@linux-mandrake.com
with "info [listname]" in the body of the message.

Optionally, you can use the web interface to subscribe to or unsubscribe
from either list:

  http://www.linux-mandrake.com/en/flists.php3#security

Cross-Ref:		Bugtraq ID 2193
Title:			arp
________________________________________________________________________________

IN NO EVENT WILL SUN MICROSYSTEMS, INC. BE LIABLE FOR ANY LOST REVENUE,

OR PUNITIVE DAMAGES HOWEVER CAUSED AND REGARDLESS OF ANY THEORY OF LIABILITY

If any of the above provisions are held to be in violation of applicable law,
void, or unenforceable in any jurisdiction, then such provisions are waived

________________________________________________________________________________

1.  Bulletins Topics

    Sun announces the release of patches for Solaris(tm) 7, 2.6, 2.5.1,
    2.5, and 2.4 (SunOS(tm) 5.7, 5.6, 5.5.1, 5.5, and 5.4) which relate
    to a setgid vulnerability in arp.

2.  Who is Affected

    Versions of arp in Solaris prior to Solaris 8


    	Vulnerable:     	Solaris 7, 7_x86, 2.6, 2.6_x86, 2.5.1,
                                2.5.1_x86, 2.5, 2.5_x86, 2.4, 2.4_x86
    	Not vulnerable:		Solaris 8.

3.  Understanding the Vulnerability

    The arp program displays and modifies the Internet-to-Ethernet address
    translation tables used by the address resolution protocol (arp).  Prior
    to Solaris 8, arp was setgid making it susceptible to certain setgid
    attacks.

    A malicious user could overflow the stack and execute shellcode which
    could allow unauthorized root access.

4.  List of Patches

    The following patches are available in relation to the above problem.

    OS Version		Patch ID
    __________		_________
    SunOS 5.7		109709-01
    SunOS 5.7_x86    	109710-01
    SunOS 5.6		109719-01
    SunOS 5.6_x86	109720-01
    SunOS 5.5.1		109721-01
    SunOS 5.5.1_x86	109722-01
    SunOS 5.5		109707-01
    SunOS 5.5_x86	109708-01
    SunOS 5.4 	        109723-01
    SunOS 5.4_x86	109724-01

APPENDICES

    ftp://sunsolve.sun.com/pub/patches/CHECKSUMS

    http://sunsolve.sun.com/security

D.  Sun Security Coordination Team's PGP key is available at:

    http://sunsolve.sun.com/pgpkey.txt

E.  To report or inquire about a security problem with Sun software, contact
    one or more of the following:

        - Your local Sun answer centers
        - Your representative computer security response team, such as CERT
        - Sun Security Coordination Team. Send email to:

     		security-alert@sun.com

F.  To receive information or subscribe to our CWS (Customer Warning System)
    mailing list, send email to:

    		security-alert@sun.com

    with a subject line (not body) containing one of the following commands:

        Command         Information Returned/Action Taken
        _______         _________________________________

        help            An explanation of how to get information

        key             Sun Security Coordination Team's PGP key

        list            A list of current security topics

        query [topic]   The email is treated as an inquiry and is forwarded to
                        the Security Coordination Team

        report [topic]  The email is treated as a security report and is
                        forwarded to the Security Coordination Team. Please
                        encrypt sensitive mail using Sun Security Coordination
                        Team's PGP key

        send topic      A short status summary or bulletin. For example, to
                        retrieve a Security Bulletin #00138, supply the
                        following in the subject line (not body):

                                send #138

        subscribe       Sender is added to our mailing list.  To subscribe,
                        supply the following in the subject line (not body):

                            	subscribe cws your-email-address

                        Note that your-email-address should be substituted
                        by your email address.

        unsubscribe     Sender is removed from the CWS mailing list.

<font size=3D"3"=3E<b=3E<A HREF=3D"mailto:feedback@gamespy=2Ecom"=3EToo Many=
 MMORPGs!</a=3E</b=3E</font=3E<br=3E
</font=3E

<!-- Fargo Image --=3E
<img src=3D"http://www=2Egamespy=2Ecom/dailymail/fargo/Fargoviking=2Egif" WI=
DTH=3D120 HEIGHT=3D120 alt=3D"Yo=2E" border=3D"0"=3E
<!-- /Fargo Image --=3E

<td width=3D"100%"=3E
<font size=3D"2"=3E
Today <A HREF=3D"http://www=2Erpgplanet=2Ecom"=3ERPGPlanet</A=3E posted a <A=
 HREF=3D"http://www=2Erpgplanet=2Ecom/features/firstlooks/dawn/"=3Epreview o=
f <I=3EDawn</I=3E</A=3E, a massively multiplayer online fantasy roleplaying =
game=2E The catch here is that Dawn will start out with no cities or nations=
 or plots or storylines; it will be <I=3Eentirely</I=3E player-driven=2E

<P=3EThe old cranky gamer in me (pictured, left) is itching to speak his min=
d=2E I've heard all these promises before -- promises of a monster ecology, =
no respawning, etc=2E etc=2E Someday I've no doubt we'll see it, but after s=
o many broken promises I'm going to wait until such a game is on shelves bef=
ore I believe any of it=2E Imagine, on a practical sense, how to balance the=
 rate of players killing monsters against the rate of monster breeding=2E No=
w, imagine doing all of that in a world that's completely undefined, where p=
layers will be building the cities and plotlines=2E That's a herculean task,=
 one that the resources of Origin and EA could hardly tackle! 

<P=3EAnother problem with MMORPG's is that the user experience is dependant =
on the number of players, and there are roughly <I=3Ea hundred</I=3E massive=
 multiplayer games in development -- many with a "swords and sorcery" theme=2E=
 If all of them charged monthly fees to play, only a handful -- perhaps half=
 a dozen -- would ever be able to support a worthwhile player base=2E  

<P=3EBut the hopeful, optomistic gamer in me (not pictured) is constantly lo=
oking for a small developer to change the face of gaming=2E Besides, it's ea=
sy to criticise a game that isn't out yet=2E What do <I=3Eyou</I=3E think=3F=
 Ridiculous vaporware hype or a good idea set to take over the world=3F <A H=
REF=3D"mailto:feedback@gamespy=2Ecom"=3EMail us your thoughts</A=3E! &nbsp; =
&nbsp; &nbsp;  -<A HREF=3D"mailto:Fargo@gamespy=2Ecom"=3EFargo</A=3E
</font=3E
</td=3E

ure that my art-rambles actually make sense=2E They've also been great at fi=

 [<A HREF=3D"#headline253827"=3Eback to headlines</A=3E]<A NAME=3D"253825"=3E=
</A=3E<P=3E<B=3EStar Wars Galaxies FAQ Updated</B=3E - Prophet<BR=3EAs is th=
e custom on Fridays, the official <a href=3D"http://www=2Estation=2Esony=2Ec=
om/starwars/FAQ=2Ejhtml"=3EStar Wars Galaxies FAQ</a=3E has been updated wit=
h answers to two new questions=2E Here they are in their entirety:


<blockquote=3E<b=3EQuestion</b=3E: Will my character's species affect my ski=
ll selection=3F<br=3E<br=3E

<b=3EAnswer</b=3E: No=2E We feel that players in Star Wars Galaxies should h=
ave the freedom to create the characters that they want, regardless of speci=
es=2E In addition, species in Star Wars are generally as diverse as we human=
s, and we want to capture that feel=2E We don't want to pigeonhole any chara=
cter into pre-defined roles, so you will be able to select from most skills =
available regardless of species=2E However, some species may receive modifie=
rs to skills based on what they are naturally good (or bad) at doing, and a =
handful of skills could be limited to specific species if there is a logical=
, Star Wars-based reason for doing so (we might decide that only Wookiees ca=
n build and repair bowcasters, for example)=2E<br=3E<br=3E

<b=3EQuestion</b=3E: Will there be custom moves and animations in combat=3F<=
br=3E<br=3E

<b=3EAnswer</b=3E: Yes=2E We are planning to make combat as exciting as poss=
ible by including specific moves and attacks with unique animations=2E From =
a design perspective, these moves will also be useful and add an element of =
strategy to everything from a simple slugfest to a shoot-out with stormtroop=
ers=2E Some moves might enhance a character's defensive capabilities or incr=
ease the damage done by an attack, for example=2E Special moves won't just l=
ook cool - they'll also be a vital part of combat=2E</blockquote=3E

BIG NEWS
________________________

OVER 300 YAHOO! GEOCITIES EXPERTS
What a success! Over the past few months over 300 members have volunteered 
to become Yahoo! GeoCities Experts and helped thousands build great sites. 
Yahoo! Experts is a question-and-answer service where you can seek expert advice 
on building GeoCities pages, selecting wine at a restaurant, or just about 
anything. Check it out!
http://experts.yahoo.com/topics/yahoo__geocities-383000187 


SHARE YOUR HOLIDAY MEMORIES
Want to share your stack of holiday photos with friends near and far? 
Let Yahoo! GeoCities help with PageWizards photo templates. Simply fill 
in the blank and build a professional-looking photo page in minutes. You can 
include a message and up to four photos with captions. 
http://geocities.yahoo.com/members/wizards/photopage_launch.html 


TAKE THE TOUR
Need help getting your site up and running? Want to learn what Yahoo! GeoCities 
has to offer? Check out our new GeoCities Tour. Learn about our editors, as well 
as how to update, enhance and drive traffic to your site.
http://help.yahoo.com/help/us/geo/tour/tour-01.html 

SITE STATISTICS -TRACK VISITS TO YOUR SITE
If you've ever wondered which pages on your site are most popular or where most of 
your visitors are coming from, then Yahoo! GeoCities Sites Statistics is for you! 
Our new automatic and easy-to-read reports show you detailed information about page 
views, user profiles and the web sites referring the most visitors to your site. 
http://us.geocities.yahoo.com/stats 

PROMOTE YOUR PAGE
Drive more traffic to your site by listing it in our Member Pages directory. With 
thousands of categories to choose from, you can list your web page in the right place 
for potential visitors to find you. And you'll also receive preferred placement in the 
Yahoo! GeoCities search engine. Watch your traffic grow! 
http://pages.yahoo.com 


________________________

SITE PROMOTION TIP
________________________

The name says it all. Whatever you put between your page's <title> tags will be 
displayed by search engines, directories and bookmark lists across the Web. 
Help visitors find and understand what your site is about by giving your pages specific 
names. Check out our example. 

<title> Recipes of Southern Turkey </title>

________________________

JavaScript Trick
________________________

Creating navigation within your site has never been easier! By using simple JavaScript, 
you can create dynamic links that return visitors to the last page they viewed. To do 
this you use the visitor's "history". History is a list of web sites that an individual 
browser has visited. 

Here's the code:

<a href="#" 
onClick="history.back();">Go Back</a>

SITE SPOTLIGHT
________________________

GUINEA PIG ZERO
Guinea Pig Zero is an "occupational jobzine for people who volunteer as 
medical or pharmaceutical research subjects." Sign your waivers, take your 
number, swallow your pills, and dive in.
http://www.geocities.com/gpigzero/

ROBIN HOOD - BOLD OUTLAW OF BANSDALE AND SHERWOOD
How much do you know about Robin Hood? If you know nothing more than he robs 
from the rich and gives to the poor, then you've come to the right place. 
Here, you'll find an introduction to the man, his legend, and his band of 
merry men. But was there ever a real Robin Hood? This site also takes a shot 
at discovering the true identity of Robin. 
http://www.geocities.com/puckrobin/rh/

TOLERANCE 4 KIDS 
Traditionally, the subjects of diversity, civil rights, tolerance, and the 
Holocaust were reserved for middle school students and up. However, it is 
increasingly important that kids learn even earlier about the dangers of hate, 
racism, and prejudice. This web site introduces kids to these issues and teaches 
them ways to help stop hate. Note: this site is designed for use with parental 
guidance and is appropriate for ages 8 and up.
http://www.geocities.com/tolerance4kids/

MAXIMUM RUSSELL CROWE
>From tobacco industry executive in The Insider to centurion fighter in Gladiator, 
Russell Crowe is definitely one of the hottest names in show biz. To get the inside 
scoop on this Aussie heartthrob, check out Maximum Russell Crowe. This site includes 
extensive news, biographical information, photos, fan reviews, and interviews.
http://www.geocities.com/maximumcrowe/

GEOSTORY
_____________________

Each month we like to publish a story that shows how Yahoo! 
GeoCities affects peoples lives. Heres our pick for this month:

Dear GeoStory,

I always wanted to put up a site for my metal band in England, but I 
thought I'd never be able to do it, but thanks to your PageBuilder it 
was a snap. I can advertise my band and best of all it's free. It makes a 
real difference to be in a band and be able to say, "visit the web site". 
Fantastic. The easy to use PageBuilder allowed me to make a professional 
site with many pages all linked up; I have counters and soon a guest book. 
Thanks a bunch, and be assured that I will spread the news and thanks for 
being a great service to up-and-coming bands. 

Mike
http://www.geocities.com/nadir666us/nadir666us.html  
 

Do you have a story of your own about how Yahoo! GeoCities has
influenced your life? If youd like to share it with us and other
Homesteaders, send it to geostory@yahoo.com

<table width=150 border=0 cellspacing=0 cellpadding=4><tr bgcolor=003399><td colspan=2><font face=Arial size=-1 color=white><b>JavaScript Trick</b></font></td></tr><tr bgcolor=eeeeee><td colspan=2><font face=Arial size=-1>
Creating navigation within your site has never been easier! By using simple JavaScript, you can create dynamic links that return visitors to the last page they viewed. To do this you use the visitor's "history". History is a list of web sites that an individual browser has visited. <p>Click the link below to see how the javascript link works.
<p><center><a href="#" onClick="history.back();"><b>Go Back</b></a></center> <p>
Here's the code:</font><p><font face="Courier" size=-1>
<center>&#060;a href="#" <br>onClick= <nobr>"history.back();</nobr> "&gt;Go Back&#060;&#047;a&gt;</center>
